         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Wadi_Shab_(6).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Wadi Shab
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Oman lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/16th_parallel_north" title="16th parallel north">16°</a> and <a href="/wiki/28th_parallel_north" title="28th parallel north">28°&nbsp;N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/52nd_meridian_east" title="52nd meridian east">52°</a> and <a href="/wiki/60th_meridian_east" title="60th meridian east">60°&nbsp;E</a>. A vast gravel desert plain covers most of central Oman, with mountain ranges along the north (<a href="/wiki/Al_Hajar_Mountains" title="Al Hajar Mountains">Al Hajar Mountains</a>) and southeast coast (<a href="/wiki/Dhofar_Mountains" title="Dhofar Mountains">Qara or Dhofar Mountains</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[112]</a></sup> where the country's main cities are located: the capital city <a href="/wiki/Muscat,_Oman" class="mw-redirect" title="Muscat, Oman">Muscat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sohar" title="Sohar">Sohar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sur,_Oman" title="Sur, Oman">Sur</a> in the north, and <a href="/wiki/Salalah" title="Salalah">Salalah</a> in the south. Oman's climate is hot and dry in the interior and humid along the coast. During past epochs, Oman was covered by ocean, as evidenced by the large numbers of fossilized shells found in areas of the desert away from the modern coastline. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Oman-Oasis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Oman-Oasis.jpg/220px-Oman-Oasis.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Oman-Oasis.jpg/330px-Oman-Oasis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Oman-Oasis.jpg/440px-Oman-Oasis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Oman-Oasis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An Omani desert landscape
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The peninsula of <a href="/wiki/Musandam_Peninsula" title="Musandam Peninsula">Musandam</a> (Musandem) <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">exclave</a>, which is strategically located on the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Hormuz" title="Strait of Hormuz">Strait of Hormuz</a>, is separated from the rest of Oman by the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jkrogh_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jkrogh-115">[113]</a></sup> The series of small towns known collectively as <a href="/wiki/Dibba" title="Dibba">Dibba</a> are the gateway to the Musandam peninsula on land and the fishing villages of Musandam by sea, with boats available for hire at <a href="/wiki/Khasab" title="Khasab">Khasab</a> for trips into the Musandam peninsula by sea. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:SurOman.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/SurOman.jpg/220px-SurOman.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/SurOman.jpg/330px-SurOman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/SurOman.jpg/440px-SurOman.jpg 2x" data-file-width="772" data-file-height="512"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:SurOman.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The coast of <a href="/wiki/Sur,_Oman" title="Sur, Oman">Sur, Oman</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Oman's other exclave, inside UAE territory, known as <a href="/wiki/Madha" title="Madha">Madha</a>, located halfway between the Musandam Peninsula and the main body of Oman,<sup id="cite_ref-jkrogh_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jkrogh-115">[113]</a></sup> is part of the Musandam governorate, covering approximately 75&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (29&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). Madha's boundary was settled in 1969, with the north-east corner of Madha barely 10&nbsp;m (32.8&nbsp;ft) from the <a href="/wiki/Fujairah" title="Fujairah">Fujairah</a> road. Within the Madha exclave is a UAE <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">enclave</a> called <a href="/wiki/Nahwa" title="Nahwa">Nahwa</a>, belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Sharjah" title="Emirate of Sharjah">Emirate of Sharjah</a>, situated about 8&nbsp;km (5&nbsp;mi) along a dirt track west of the town of New Madha, and consisting of about forty houses with a clinic and telephone exchange.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The central desert of Oman is an important source of <a href="/wiki/Meteorites" class="mw-redirect" title="Meteorites">meteorites</a> for scientific analysis.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Salalah_during_khareef.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Salalah_during_khareef.jpg/220px-Salalah_during_khareef.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Salalah_during_khareef.jpg/330px-Salalah_during_khareef.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Salalah_during_khareef.jpg/440px-Salalah_during_khareef.jpg 2x" data-file-width="627" data-file-height="470"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Salalah_during_khareef.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Salalah during Khareef Season (June to September)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Oman" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Oman">Climate of Oman</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Like the rest of the Persian Gulf, Oman generally has one of the hottest climates in the world—with summer temperatures in Muscat and northern Oman averaging 30 to 40&nbsp;°C (86.0 to 104.0&nbsp;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup> Oman receives <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Oman" title="Geography of Oman">little rainfall</a>, with annual rainfall in Muscat averaging 100&nbsp;mm (3.9&nbsp;in), occurring mostly in January. In the south, the <a href="/wiki/Dhofar" class="mw-redirect" title="Dhofar">Dhofar</a> Mountains area near Salalah has a tropical-like climate and receives seasonal rainfall from late June to late September as a result of monsoon winds from the Indian Ocean, leaving the summer air saturated with cool moisture and heavy fog.<sup id="cite_ref-faopasture_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faopasture-119">[117]</a></sup> Summer temperatures in <a href="/wiki/Salalah" title="Salalah">Salalah</a> range from 20 to 30&nbsp;°C (68.0 to 86.0&nbsp;°F)—relatively cool compared to northern Oman.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The mountain areas receive more rainfall, and annual rainfall on the higher parts of the <a href="/wiki/Jebel_Akhdar_(Oman)" title="Jebel Akhdar (Oman)">Jabal Akhdar</a> probably exceeds 400&nbsp;mm (15.7&nbsp;in).<sup id="cite_ref-bbcweather_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcweather-121">[119]</a></sup> Low temperatures in the mountainous areas leads to snow cover once every few years.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup> Some parts of the coast, particularly near the island of <a href="/wiki/Masirah" class="mw-redirect" title="Masirah">Masirah</a>, sometimes receive no rain at all within the course of a year. The climate is generally very hot, with temperatures reaching around 54&nbsp;°C (129.2&nbsp;°F) (peak) in the hot season, from May to September.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup> Drought and limited rainfall contribute to shortages in the nation's water supply. Maintaining an adequate supply of water for agricultural and domestic use is one of Oman's most pressing environmental problems, with limited renewable <a href="/wiki/Water_resources" title="Water resources">water resources</a>. </p>
      <p>On 26 June 2018 the city of <a href="/wiki/Qurayyat,_Oman" title="Qurayyat, Oman">Qurayyat</a> set the record for highest minimum temperature in a 24-hour period, 42.6&nbsp;°C (108.7&nbsp;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In terms of climate action, major challenges remain to be solved, per the United Nations Sustainable Development 2019 index. The <span class="nowrap"><span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br>2</span></span></span> emissions from energy (t<span class="nowrap"><span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br>2</span></span></span>/capita) and <span class="nowrap"><span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br>2</span></span></span> emissions embodied in fossil fuel exports (kg per capita) rates are very high, while imported <span class="nowrap"><span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br>2</span></span></span> emissions (t<span class="nowrap"><span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br>2</span></span></span>/capita) and people affected by climate-related disasters (per 100,000 people) rates are low.<sup id="cite_ref-UNSD3_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNSD3-125">[123]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Oman" title="Wildlife of Oman">Wildlife of Oman</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nakhalfarms.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Nakhalfarms.jpg/220px-Nakhalfarms.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Nakhalfarms.jpg/330px-Nakhalfarms.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Nakhalfarms.jpg/440px-Nakhalfarms.jpg 2x" data-file-width="659" data-file-height="431"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nakhalfarms.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Nakhal palm tree farms in Oman's <a href="/wiki/Al_Batinah_Region" title="Al Batinah Region">Batina Region</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The-Worlds-Most-Isolated-and-Distinct-Whale-Population-Humpback-Whales-of-the-Arabian-Sea-pone.0114162.s001.tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/The-Worlds-Most-Isolated-and-Distinct-Whale-Population-Humpback-Whales-of-the-Arabian-Sea-pone.0114162.s001.tif/lossy-page1-220px-The-Worlds-Most-Isolated-and-Distinct-Whale-Population-Humpback-Whales-of-the-Arabian-Sea-pone.0114162.s001.tif.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="87" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/The-Worlds-Most-Isolated-and-Distinct-Whale-Population-Humpback-Whales-of-the-Arabian-Sea-pone.0114162.s001.tif/lossy-page1-330px-The-Worlds-Most-Isolated-and-Distinct-Whale-Population-Humpback-Whales-of-the-Arabian-Sea-pone.0114162.s001.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/The-Worlds-Most-Isolated-and-Distinct-Whale-Population-Humpback-Whales-of-the-Arabian-Sea-pone.0114162.s001.tif/lossy-page1-440px-The-Worlds-Most-Isolated-and-Distinct-Whale-Population-Humpback-Whales-of-the-Arabian-Sea-pone.0114162.s001.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1337" data-file-height="526"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The-Worlds-Most-Isolated-and-Distinct-Whale-Population-Humpback-Whales-of-the-Arabian-Sea-pone.0114162.s001.tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Arabian <a href="/wiki/Humpback_whales" class="mw-redirect" title="Humpback whales">humpback whales</a> off <a href="/wiki/Dhofar" class="mw-redirect" title="Dhofar">Dhofar</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Desert_shrub" class="mw-redirect" title="Desert shrub">Desert shrub</a> and desert grass, common to southern Arabia, are found in Oman, but vegetation is sparse in the interior plateau, which is largely <a href="/wiki/Gravel" title="Gravel">gravel</a> desert. The greater monsoon rainfall in Dhofar and the mountains makes the growth there more luxuriant during summer; <a href="/wiki/Coconut_palm" class="mw-redirect" title="Coconut palm">coconut palms</a> grow plentifully on the coastal plains of Dhofar and <a href="/wiki/Frankincense" title="Frankincense">frankincense</a> is produced in the hills, with abundant <a href="/wiki/Oleander" class="mw-redirect" title="Oleander">oleander</a> and varieties of <a href="/wiki/Acacia" title="Acacia">acacia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Al_Hajar_Mountains" title="Al Hajar Mountains">Al Hajar Mountains</a> are a distinct <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a>, the highest points in eastern Arabia with <a href="/wiki/Wildlife" title="Wildlife">wildlife</a> including the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_tahr" title="Arabian tahr">Arabian tahr</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Indigenous_(ecology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Indigenous (ecology)">Indigenous</a> <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammals</a> include the <a href="/wiki/Leopard" title="Leopard">leopard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyena" title="Hyena">hyena</a>, fox, <a href="/wiki/Wolf" title="Wolf">wolf</a>, hare, oryx and <a href="/wiki/Ibex" title="Ibex">ibex</a>. Birds include the vulture, eagle, stork, bustard, Arabian partridge, bee eater, falcon and sunbird. In 2001, Oman had nine endangered species of mammals, five endangered types of birds,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and nineteen threatened <a href="/wiki/Plant_species" class="mw-redirect" title="Plant species">plant species</a>. Decrees have been passed to protect endangered species, including the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_leopard" title="Arabian leopard">Arabian leopard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabian_oryx" title="Arabian oryx">Arabian oryx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountain_gazelle" title="Mountain gazelle">mountain gazelle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goitered_gazelle" title="Goitered gazelle">goitered gazelle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabian_tahr" title="Arabian tahr">Arabian tahr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_sea_turtle" title="Green sea turtle">green sea turtle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hawksbill_turtle" class="mw-redirect" title="Hawksbill turtle">hawksbill turtle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Olive_ridley_turtle" class="mw-redirect" title="Olive ridley turtle">olive ridley turtle</a>. However, the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Oryx_Sanctuary" title="Arabian Oryx Sanctuary">Arabian Oryx Sanctuary</a> is the first site ever to be deleted from <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>'s World Heritage List, following the government's 2007 decision to reduce the site's area by 90% in order to clear the way for oil prospectors.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Osprey_yiti.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Osprey_yiti.jpg/170px-Osprey_yiti.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Osprey_yiti.jpg/255px-Osprey_yiti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Osprey_yiti.jpg/340px-Osprey_yiti.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1884" data-file-height="2377"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Osprey_yiti.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Osprey in Yiti Beach, Oman
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Local and national entities have noted unethical treatment of animals in Oman. In particular, stray dogs (and to a lesser extent, stray cats) are often the victims of torture, abuse or neglect.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup> The only approved method of decreasing the stray dog population is shooting by police officers. The Oman government has refused to implement a spay and neuter programme or create any animal shelters in the country. Cats, while seen as more acceptable than dogs, are viewed as pests and frequently die of starvation or illness.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In recent years, Oman has become one of the newer hot spots for <a href="/wiki/Whale_watching" title="Whale watching">whale watching</a>, highlighting the critically endangered Arabian <a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">humpback whale</a>, the most isolated and only non-<a href="/wiki/Animal_migration" title="Animal migration">migratory</a> population in the world, <a href="/wiki/Sperm_whale" title="Sperm whale">sperm whales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pygmy_blue_whale" title="Pygmy blue whale">pygmy blue whales</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Oman" title="Politics of Oman">Politics of Oman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Oman" title="Human rights in Oman">Human rights in Oman</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Oman-Muscat-16-Sultans-Palace-2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Oman-Muscat-16-Sultans-Palace-2.JPG/220px-Oman-Muscat-16-Sultans-Palace-2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Oman-Muscat-16-Sultans-Palace-2.JPG/330px-Oman-Muscat-16-Sultans-Palace-2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Oman-Muscat-16-Sultans-Palace-2.JPG/440px-Oman-Muscat-16-Sultans-Palace-2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Oman-Muscat-16-Sultans-Palace-2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Sultan's <a href="/wiki/Al_Alam_Palace" title="Al Alam Palace">Al Alam Palace</a> in Old Muscat
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Oman is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a> and an <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-oman-abs_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oman-abs-131">[129]</a></sup> in which all legislative, executive and judiciary power ultimately rests in the hands of the hereditary Sultan. Consequently, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> has routinely rated the country "Not Free".<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The sultan is the head of state and directly controls the foreign affairs and defence portfolios.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup> He has absolute power and issues <a href="/wiki/Rule_by_decree" title="Rule by decree">laws by decree</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fh12_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fh12-134">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-econwut_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econwut-135">[133]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_system">Legal system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Legal system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Oman is an <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a>, with the Sultan's word having the force of law. The judiciary branch is subordinate to the Sultan. According to Oman's constitution, <a href="/wiki/Sharia_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharia law">Sharia law</a> is one of the sources of legislation. Sharia court departments within the civil court system are responsible for family-law matters, such as divorce and inheritance. </p>
      <p>Oman does not have <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">separation of powers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> All power is concentrated in the Sultan,<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> who is also chief of staff of the armed forces, Minister of Defence, Minister of Foreign Affairs and chairman of the Central Bank.<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> All legislation since 1970 has been promulgated through royal decrees, including the 1996 Basic Law.<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> The Sultan appoints judges, and can grant pardons and commute sentences.<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> The Sultan's authority is inviolable and the Sultan expects total subordination to his will.<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The administration of justice is highly personalized, with limited due process protections, especially in political and security-related cases.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Basic_Statute_of_Oman" title="Basic Statute of Oman">Basic Statute of the State</a><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup> is supposedly the cornerstone of the Omani legal system and it operates as a constitution for the country. The Basic Statute was issued in 1996 and thus far has only been amended once, in 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup> in response to <a href="/wiki/2011_Omani_protests" title="2011 Omani protests">protests</a>. </p>
      <p>Though Oman's legal code theoretically protects civil liberties and personal freedoms, both are regularly ignored by the regime.<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> Women and children face legal discrimination in many areas.<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> Women are excluded from certain state benefits, such as housing loans, and are refused equal rights under the personal status law.<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> Women also experience restrictions on their self-determination in respect to health and reproductive rights.<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gates_%26_Qaboos_of_Oman_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Gates_%26_Qaboos_of_Oman_cropped.jpg/170px-Gates_%26_Qaboos_of_Oman_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Gates_%26_Qaboos_of_Oman_cropped.jpg/255px-Gates_%26_Qaboos_of_Oman_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Gates_%26_Qaboos_of_Oman_cropped.jpg/340px-Gates_%26_Qaboos_of_Oman_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2243" data-file-height="2747"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gates_%26_Qaboos_of_Oman_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Former Sultan <a href="/wiki/Qaboos_bin_Said_al_Said" class="mw-redirect" title="Qaboos bin Said al Said">Qaboos bin Said al Said</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Omani legislature is the bicameral <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Oman" title="Council of Oman">Council of Oman</a>, consisting of an upper chamber, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_State_(Oman)" title="Council of State (Oman)">Council of State</a> (Majlis ad-Dawlah) and a lower chamber, the <a href="/wiki/Consultative_Assembly_of_Oman" class="mw-redirect" title="Consultative Assembly of Oman">Consultative Council</a> (Majlis ash-Shoura).<sup id="cite_ref-arparl_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arparl-139">[137]</a></sup> Political parties are banned.<sup id="cite_ref-econwut_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econwut-135">[133]</a></sup> The upper chamber has 71 members, appointed by the Sultan from among prominent Omanis; it has only advisory powers.<sup id="cite_ref-cialegbr_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cialegbr-140">[138]</a></sup> The 84 members of the Consultative Council are elected by popular vote to serve four-year terms, but the Sultan makes the final selections and can negotiate the election results.<sup id="cite_ref-cialegbr_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cialegbr-140">[138]</a></sup> The members are appointed for three-year terms, which may be renewed once.<sup id="cite_ref-arparl_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arparl-139">[137]</a></sup> The last elections were held on <a href="/wiki/2019_Omani_general_election" title="2019 Omani general election">27 October 2019</a>, and the next is due in October 2023. Oman's national anthem, <i><a href="/wiki/As-Salam_as-Sultani" title="As-Salam as-Sultani">As-Salam as-Sultani</a></i> is dedicated to former Sultan Qaboos. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_policy">Foreign policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Foreign policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Oman" title="Foreign relations of Oman">Foreign relations of Oman</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Walks_With_Omani_Qaboos_bin_Said_Al_Said.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Secretary_Kerry_Walks_With_Omani_Qaboos_bin_Said_Al_Said.jpg/220px-Secretary_Kerry_Walks_With_Omani_Qaboos_bin_Said_Al_Said.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Secretary_Kerry_Walks_With_Omani_Qaboos_bin_Said_Al_Said.jpg/330px-Secretary_Kerry_Walks_With_Omani_Qaboos_bin_Said_Al_Said.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Secretary_Kerry_Walks_With_Omani_Qaboos_bin_Said_Al_Said.jpg/440px-Secretary_Kerry_Walks_With_Omani_Qaboos_bin_Said_Al_Said.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2784" data-file-height="1848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Walks_With_Omani_Qaboos_bin_Said_Al_Said.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>U.S. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> meets with Sultan Qaboos in Muscat, May 2013.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since 1970, Oman has pursued a moderate foreign policy, and has expanded its diplomatic relations dramatically. Oman is among the very few Arab countries that have maintained friendly ties with <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pop_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop-141">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/WikiLeaks" title="WikiLeaks">WikiLeaks</a> disclosed US diplomatic cables which state that Oman helped free British sailors captured by Iran's navy in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup> The same cables also portray the Omani government as wishing to maintain cordial relations with Iran, and as having consistently resisted US diplomatic pressure to adopt a sterner stance.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yusuf_bin_Alawi_bin_Abdullah" title="Yusuf bin Alawi bin Abdullah">Yusuf bin Alawi bin Abdullah</a> is the Sultanate's Minister Responsible for Foreign Affairs. </p>
      <p>Oman allowed the British <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indian_Navy" title="Indian Navy">Indian Navy</a> access to the port facilities of <a href="/wiki/Al_Duqm_Port_%26_Drydock" title="Al Duqm Port &amp; Drydock">Al Duqm Port &amp; Drydock</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ie_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ie-147">[145]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sultan_of_Oman%27s_Armed_Forces" title="Sultan of Oman's Armed Forces">Sultan of Oman's Armed Forces</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Portsmouth_korvet_Al-Shamikh_Oman_18-10-2011_15-15-51.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Portsmouth_korvet_Al-Shamikh_Oman_18-10-2011_15-15-51.png/300px-Portsmouth_korvet_Al-Shamikh_Oman_18-10-2011_15-15-51.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Portsmouth_korvet_Al-Shamikh_Oman_18-10-2011_15-15-51.png/450px-Portsmouth_korvet_Al-Shamikh_Oman_18-10-2011_15-15-51.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Portsmouth_korvet_Al-Shamikh_Oman_18-10-2011_15-15-51.png/600px-Portsmouth_korvet_Al-Shamikh_Oman_18-10-2011_15-15-51.png 2x" data-file-width="3996" data-file-height="2248"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Portsmouth_korvet_Al-Shamikh_Oman_18-10-2011_15-15-51.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Khareef-class_corvette" title="Khareef-class corvette">Khareef-class corvette</a>, Al-Shamikh
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_International_Peace_Research_Institute" title="Stockholm International Peace Research Institute">SIPRI</a>'s estimation of Oman's military and security expenditure as a percentage of GDP in 2019 was 8.8 percent,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup> making it the world's highest rate in that year, higher than <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> (8 percent).<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup> Oman's on-average military spending as a percentage of GDP between 2016 and 2018 was around 10 percent, while the world's average during the same period was 2.2 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-WBMS_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WBMS-150">[148]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Oman's military manpower totalled 44,100 in 2006, including 25,000 men in the army, 4,200 sailors in the navy, and an air force with 4,100 personnel. The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Household" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Household">Royal Household</a> maintained 5,000 Guards, 1,000 in Special Forces, 150 sailors in the Royal Yacht fleet, and 250 pilots and ground personnel in the Royal Flight squadrons. Oman also maintains a modestly sized paramilitary force of 4,400 men.<sup id="cite_ref-cordesman_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cordesman-151">[149]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Army_of_Oman" title="Royal Army of Oman">Royal Army of Oman</a> had 25,000 active personnel in 2006, plus a small contingent of Royal Household troops. Despite a comparative large military spending, it has been relatively slow to modernise its forces. Oman has a relatively limited number of tanks, including 6 <a href="/wiki/M60A1" class="mw-redirect" title="M60A1">M60A1</a>, 73 <a href="/wiki/M60A3" class="mw-redirect" title="M60A3">M60A3</a> and 38 <a href="/wiki/Challenger_2" title="Challenger 2">Challenger 2</a> main battle tanks, as well as 37 aging <a href="/wiki/FV101_Scorpion" title="FV101 Scorpion">Scorpion</a> light tanks.<sup id="cite_ref-cordesman_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cordesman-151">[149]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force_of_Oman" title="Royal Air Force of Oman">Royal Air Force of Oman</a> has approximately 4,100 men, with only 36 combat aircraft and no armed helicopters. Combat aircraft include 20 aging <a href="/wiki/SEPECAT_Jaguar" title="SEPECAT Jaguar">Jaguars</a>, 12 <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Hawk" title="BAE Systems Hawk">Hawk</a> Mk 203s, 4 Hawk Mk 103s and 12 <a href="/wiki/PC-9" class="mw-redirect" title="PC-9">PC-9</a> turboprop trainers with a limited combat capability. It has one squadron of 12 <a href="/wiki/F-16" class="mw-redirect" title="F-16">F-16</a>C/D aircraft. Oman also has 4 <a href="/wiki/FFA_AS-202_Bravo" class="mw-redirect" title="FFA AS-202 Bravo">A202-18 Bravos</a> and 8 <a href="/wiki/PAC_MFI-17_Mushshak" title="PAC MFI-17 Mushshak">MFI-17B Mushshaqs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cordesman_151-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cordesman-151">[149]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy_of_Oman" title="Royal Navy of Oman">Royal Navy of Oman</a> had 4,200 men in 2000, and is headquartered at <a href="/wiki/Seeb" title="Seeb">Seeb</a>. It has bases at Ahwi, Ghanam Island, <a href="/wiki/Mussandam" class="mw-redirect" title="Mussandam">Mussandam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salalah" title="Salalah">Salalah</a>. In 2006, Oman had 10 surface combat vessels. These included two 1,450-ton <a href="/wiki/Qahir-class_corvette" title="Qahir-class corvette"><i>Qahir</i> class</a> <a href="/wiki/Corvette" title="Corvette">corvettes</a>, and 8 ocean-going <a href="/wiki/Patrol_boat" title="Patrol boat">patrol boats</a>. The Omani Navy had one 2,500-ton <a href="/wiki/Nasr_al_Bahr_(L2)" title="Nasr al Bahr (L2)"><i>Nasr al Bahr</i> class</a> LSL (240 troops, 7 tanks) with a helicopter deck. Oman also had at least four <a href="/wiki/Landing_craft" title="Landing craft">landing craft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cordesman_151-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cordesman-151">[149]</a></sup> Oman ordered three <a href="/wiki/Khareef-class_corvette" title="Khareef-class corvette"><i>Khareef</i> class</a> corvettes from the <a href="/wiki/VT_Group" title="VT Group">VT Group</a> for £400&nbsp;million in 2007. They were built at <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth" title="Portsmouth">Portsmouth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup> In 2010 Oman spent US$4.074&nbsp;billion on military expenditures, 8.5% <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_military_expenditure_share_of_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by military expenditure share of GDP">of the gross domestic product</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup> The sultanate has a long history of association with the British military and defence industry.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/SIPRI" class="mw-redirect" title="SIPRI">SIPRI</a>, Oman was the 23rd largest arms importer from 2012 to 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Oman" title="Human rights in Oman">Human rights in Oman</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Oman" title="LGBT rights in Oman">LGBT rights in Oman</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Homosexual acts are illegal in Oman.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup> The practice of <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">torture</a> is widespread in Oman state penal institutions and has become the state's typical reaction to independent political expression.<sup id="cite_ref-torture_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-torture-157">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-prev_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prev-158">[156]</a></sup> Torture methods in use in Oman include <a href="/wiki/Mock_execution" title="Mock execution">mock execution</a>, beating, <a href="/wiki/Hooding" title="Hooding">hooding</a>, solitary confinement, subjection to extremes of temperature and to constant noise, abuse and humiliation.<sup id="cite_ref-torture_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-torture-157">[155]</a></sup> There have been numerous reports of torture and other inhumane forms of punishment perpetrated by Omani security forces on protesters and detainees.<sup id="cite_ref-bti_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bti-159">[157]</a></sup> Several prisoners detained in 2012 complained of sleep deprivation, extreme temperatures and solitary confinement.<sup id="cite_ref-report_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-160">[158]</a></sup> Omani authorities kept Sultan al-Saadi, a social media activist, in solitary confinement, denied him access to his lawyer and family, forced him to wear a black bag over his head whenever he left his cell, including when using the <a href="/wiki/Toilet_(room)" title="Toilet (room)">toilet</a>, and told him his family had "forsaken" him and asked for him to be imprisoned.<sup id="cite_ref-report_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-160">[158]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mohammed_Al-fazari.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Mohammed_Al-fazari.jpeg/170px-Mohammed_Al-fazari.jpeg" decoding="async" width="170" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Mohammed_Al-fazari.jpeg/255px-Mohammed_Al-fazari.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Mohammed_Al-fazari.jpeg/340px-Mohammed_Al-fazari.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="953" data-file-height="1334"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mohammed_Al-fazari.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Mohammed Alfazari, an exiled Omani writer and journalist now living in the UK, is an author whose <a href="/wiki/Book_censorship" title="Book censorship">books are banned</a> in Oman. He is also the founder and EIC of Muwatin.<sup id="cite_ref-omanhrw_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-omanhrw-161">[159]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Omani government decides who can or cannot be a journalist and this permission can be withdrawn at any time.<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> Censorship and <a href="/wiki/Self-censorship" title="Self-censorship">self-censorship</a> are a constant factor.<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> Omanis have limited access to political information through the media.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[161]</a></sup> Access to news and information can be problematic: journalists have to be content with news compiled by the official news agency on some issues.<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> Through a decree by the Sultan, the government has now extended its control over the media to blogs and other websites.<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> Omanis cannot hold a public meeting without the government's approval.<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> Omanis who want to set up a non-governmental organisation of any kind need a licence.<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> To get a licence, they have to demonstrate that the organisation is "for legitimate objectives" and not "inimical to the social order".<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> The Omani government does not permit the formation of independent <a href="/wiki/Civil_society" title="Civil society">civil society</a> associations.<sup id="cite_ref-bti_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bti-159">[157]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> issued on 2016, that an Omani court sentenced three journalists to prison and ordered the permanent closure of their newspaper, over an article that alleged corruption in the judiciary.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[162]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The law prohibits criticism of the Sultan and government in any form or medium.<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> Oman's police do not need <a href="/wiki/Search_warrants" class="mw-redirect" title="Search warrants">search warrants</a> to enter people's homes.<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> The law does not provide citizens with the right to change their government.<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> The Sultan retains ultimate authority on all foreign and domestic issues.<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> Government officials are not subject to financial disclosure laws.<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> Libel laws and concerns for national security have been used to suppress criticism of government figures and politically objectionable views.<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> Publication of books is limited and the government restricts their importation and distribution, as with other media products.<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Merely mentioning the existence of such restrictions can land Omanis in trouble.<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> In 2009, a web publisher was fined and given a suspended jail sentence for revealing that a supposedly live TV programme was actually pre-recorded to eliminate any criticisms of the government.<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Faced with so many restrictions, Omanis have resorted to unconventional methods for expressing their views.<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> Omanis sometimes use donkeys to express their views.<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> Writing about Gulf rulers in 2001, Dale Eickelman observed: "Only in Oman has the occasional donkey… been used as a mobile billboard to express anti-regime sentiments. There is no way in which police can maintain dignity in seizing and destroying a donkey on whose flank a political message has been inscribed."<sup id="cite_ref-qaboos_162-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qaboos-162">[160]</a></sup> Some people have been <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_misinformation#Efforts_to_combat_misinformation" title="COVID-19 misinformation">arrested</a> for allegedly spreading <a href="/wiki/Fake_news" title="Fake news">fake news</a> about the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Oman" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Oman">COVID-19 pandemic in Oman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[163]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Omani citizens need government permission to marry foreigners.<sup id="cite_ref-report_160-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-160">[158]</a></sup> The Ministry of Interior requires Omani citizens to obtain permission to marry foreigners (except nationals of GCC countries); permission is not automatically granted.<sup id="cite_ref-report_160-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-160">[158]</a></sup> Citizen marriage to a foreigner abroad without ministry approval may result in denial of entry for the foreign spouse at the border and preclude children from claiming citizenship rights.<sup id="cite_ref-report_160-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-160">[158]</a></sup> It also may result in a bar from government employment and a fine of 2,000 rials ($5,200).<sup id="cite_ref-report_160-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-160">[158]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nizwa_goat_market_(7).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Nizwa_goat_market_%287%29.jpg/170px-Nizwa_goat_market_%287%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Nizwa_goat_market_%287%29.jpg/255px-Nizwa_goat_market_%287%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Nizwa_goat_market_%287%29.jpg/340px-Nizwa_goat_market_%287%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1797" data-file-height="2696"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nizwa_goat_market_(7).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>According to HRW, women in Oman face discrimination.<sup id="cite_ref-omanhrw_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-omanhrw-161">[159]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In August 2014, The Omani writer and human rights defender <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mohammed_Alfazari&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mohammed Alfazari (page does not exist)">Mohammed Alfazari</a>, the founder and editor-in-chief of the e-magazine Mowatin "Citizen", disappeared after going to the police station in the Al-Qurum district of Muscat.<sup id="cite_ref-hr_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hr-166">[164]</a></sup> For several months the Omani government denied his detention and refused to disclose information about his whereabouts or condition.<sup id="cite_ref-hr_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hr-166">[164]</a></sup> On 17 July 2015, Alfazari left Oman seeking political asylum in UK after a travel ban was issued against him without providing any reasons and after his official documents including his national ID and passport were confiscated for more than 8 months.<sup id="cite_ref-cgso_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cgso-167">[165]</a></sup> There were more reports of politically motivated disappearances in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-report_160-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-160">[158]</a></sup> In 2012, armed security forces arrested Sultan al-Saadi, a social media activist.<sup id="cite_ref-report_160-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-160">[158]</a></sup> According to reports, authorities detained him at an unknown location for one month for comments he posted online critical of the government.<sup id="cite_ref-report_160-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-160">[158]</a></sup> Authorities previously arrested al-Saadi in 2011 for participating in protests and again in 2012 for posting comments online deemed insulting to Sultan Qaboos.<sup id="cite_ref-report_160-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-160">[158]</a></sup> In May 2012 security forces detained Ismael al-Meqbali, Habiba al-Hinai and Yaqoub al-Kharusi, human rights activists who were visiting striking oil workers.<sup id="cite_ref-report_160-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-160">[158]</a></sup> Authorities released al-Hinai and al-Kharusi shortly after their detention but did not inform al-Meqbali's friends and family of his whereabouts for weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-report_160-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-160">[158]</a></sup> Authorities pardoned al-Meqbali in March.<sup id="cite_ref-report_160-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-160">[158]</a></sup> In December 2013, a Yemeni national disappeared in Oman after he was arrested at a checkpoint in Dhofar Governorate.<sup id="cite_ref-alkaram_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alkaram-168">[166]</a></sup> Omani authorities refuse to acknowledge his detention.<sup id="cite_ref-alkaram_168-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alkaram-168">[166]</a></sup> His whereabouts and condition remain unknown.<sup id="cite_ref-alkaram_168-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alkaram-168">[166]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The National Human Rights Commission, established in 2008, is not independent from the regime.<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> It is chaired by the former deputy inspector general of Police and Customs and its members are appointed by royal decree.<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> In June 2012, one of its members requested that she be relieved of her duties because she disagreed with a statement made by the Commission justifying the arrest of intellectuals and bloggers and the restriction of freedom of expression in the name of respect for "the principles of religion and customs of the country".<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since the beginning of the "Omani Spring" in January 2011, a number of serious violations of civil rights have been reported, amounting to a critical deterioration of the human rights situation.<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> Prisons are inaccessible to independent monitors.<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> Members of the independent Omani Group of Human Rights have been harassed, arrested and sentenced to jail. There have been numerous testimonies of torture and other inhumane forms of punishment perpetrated by security forces on protesters and detainees.<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> The detainees were all peacefully exercising their right to freedom of expression and assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> Although authorities must obtain court orders to hold suspects in pre-trial detention, they do not regularly do this.<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> The penal code was amended in October 2011 to allow the arrest and detention of individuals without an arrest warrant from public prosecutors.<sup id="cite_ref-rule_11-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rule-11">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In January 2014, Omani intelligence agents arrested a Bahraini actor and handed him over to the Bahraini authorities on the same day of his arrest.<sup id="cite_ref-bahr_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bahr-169">[167]</a></sup> The actor has been subjected to a <a href="/wiki/Forced_disappearance" title="Forced disappearance">forced disappearance</a>. His whereabouts and condition remain unknown.<sup id="cite_ref-bahr_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bahr-169">[167]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Migrant_workers">Migrant workers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Migrant workers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Migrant_workers_in_the_Gulf_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Migrant workers in the Gulf region">Migrant workers in the Gulf region</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The plight of <a href="/wiki/Domestic_workers" class="mw-redirect" title="Domestic workers">domestic workers</a> in Oman is a taboo subject.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-taboo_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taboo-171">[169]</a></sup> In 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> government determined that out of all the countries in the Middle East, only Oman and Israel qualify as safe for Filipino migrants.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup> In 2012, it was reported that every 6 days, an Indian migrant in Oman commits suicide.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup> There has been a campaign urging authorities to check the migrant suicide rate.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup> In the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Global_Slavery_Index" title="Global Slavery Index">Global Slavery Index</a>, Oman is ranked No. 45 due to 26,000 people in <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-index_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-index-176">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[175]</a></sup> The descendants of servant tribes and slaves are victims of widespread discrimination.<sup id="cite_ref-bti_159-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bti-159">[157]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-inequal_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inequal-178">[176]</a></sup> Oman was one of the last countries to <a href="/wiki/Abolition_of_slavery_timeline" class="mw-redirect" title="Abolition of slavery timeline">abolish slavery</a>, in 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-taboo_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taboo-171">[169]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Regions_and_governorates_of_Oman" class="mw-redirect" title="Regions and governorates of Oman">Regions and governorates of Oman</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Oman,_administrative_divisions_2011_-_de_-_colored.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Oman%2C_administrative_divisions_2011_-_de_-_colored.svg/280px-Oman%2C_administrative_divisions_2011_-_de_-_colored.svg.png" decoding="async" width="280" height="365" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Oman%2C_administrative_divisions_2011_-_de_-_colored.svg/420px-Oman%2C_administrative_divisions_2011_-_de_-_colored.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Oman%2C_administrative_divisions_2011_-_de_-_colored.svg/560px-Oman%2C_administrative_divisions_2011_-_de_-_colored.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="980" data-file-height="1276"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Oman,_administrative_divisions_2011_-_de_-_colored.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Governorates of Oman
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Sultanate is administratively divided into eleven governorates. Governorates are, in turn, divided into 60 <a href="/wiki/Wilayat" class="mw-redirect" title="Wilayat">wilayats</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[177]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[178]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ad_Dakhiliyah_Governorate" title="Ad Dakhiliyah Governorate">Ad Dakhiliyah</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ad_Dhahirah_Governorate" title="Ad Dhahirah Governorate">Ad Dhahirah</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Al_Batinah_North_Governorate" title="Al Batinah North Governorate">Al Batinah North</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Al_Batinah_South_Governorate" title="Al Batinah South Governorate">Al Batinah South</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Al_Buraimi_Governorate" title="Al Buraimi Governorate">Al Buraimi</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Al_Wusta_Governorate_(Oman)" title="Al Wusta Governorate (Oman)">Al Wusta</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ash_Sharqiyah_North_Governorate" title="Ash Sharqiyah North Governorate">Ash Sharqiyah North</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ash_Sharqiyah_South_Governorate" title="Ash Sharqiyah South Governorate">Ash Sharqiyah South</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Dhofar_Governorate" title="Dhofar Governorate">Dhofar</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Muscat_Governorate" title="Muscat Governorate">Muscat</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Musandam_Governorate" title="Musandam Governorate">Musandam</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Oman" title="Economy of Oman">Economy of Oman</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Oman_Export_Treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Oman_Export_Treemap.png/300px-Oman_Export_Treemap.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Oman_Export_Treemap.png/450px-Oman_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Oman_Export_Treemap.png/600px-Oman_Export_Treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="854" data-file-height="668"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Oman_Export_Treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A proportional representation of Oman's exports
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Oman's Basic Statute of the State expresses in Article 11 that the "national economy is based on justice and the principles of a <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">free economy</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-molabs_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-molabs-181">[179]</a></sup> By regional standards, Oman has a relatively diversified economy, but remains dependent on oil exports. In terms of monetary value, mineral fuels accounted for 82.2 percent of total product exports in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-wteio_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wteio-182">[180]</a></sup> Tourism is the fastest-growing industry in Oman. Other sources of income, agriculture and industry, are small in comparison and account for less than 1% of the country's exports, but diversification is seen as a priority by the government. Agriculture, often <a href="/wiki/Subsistence" class="mw-redirect" title="Subsistence">subsistence</a> in its character, produces <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_dactylifera" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenix dactylifera">dates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lime_(fruit)" title="Lime (fruit)">limes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cereal" title="Cereal">grains</a> and vegetables, but with less than 1% of the country under <a href="/wiki/Tillage" title="Tillage">cultivation</a>, Oman is likely to remain a net importer of food. </p>
      <p>Oman's socio-economic structure is described as being hyper-centralized <a href="/wiki/Rentier_state" title="Rentier state">rentier</a> welfare state.<sup id="cite_ref-bti1_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bti1-183">[181]</a></sup> The largest 10 percent of corporations in Oman are the employers of almost 80 percent of Omani nationals in the private sector. Half of the private sector jobs are classified as elementary. One third of employed Omanis are in the private sector, while the remaining majority are in the public sector.<sup id="cite_ref-RSIO_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RSIO-184">[182]</a></sup> A hyper-centralized structure produces a monopoly-like economy, which hinders having a healthy competitive environment between businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-bti1_183-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bti1-183">[181]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since a slump in oil prices in 1998, Oman has made active plans to diversify its economy and is placing a greater emphasis on other areas of industry, namely tourism and infrastructure. Oman had a 2020 Vision to diversify the economy established in 1995, which targeted a decrease in oil's share to less than 10 percent of GDP by 2020, but it was rendered obsolete in 2011. Oman then established 2040 Vision.<sup id="cite_ref-bti1_183-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bti1-183">[181]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MSM_Main.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/MSM_Main.JPG/220px-MSM_Main.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/MSM_Main.JPG/330px-MSM_Main.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/MSM_Main.JPG/440px-MSM_Main.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3968" data-file-height="2976"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MSM_Main.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Muscat_Securities_Market" title="Muscat Securities Market">Muscat Securities Market</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A <a href="/wiki/Oman%E2%80%93United_States_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Oman–United States Free Trade Agreement">free-trade agreement with the United States</a> took effect 1 January 2009, eliminated tariff barriers on all consumer and industrial products, and also provided strong protections for foreign businesses investing in Oman.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Oman" title="Tourism in Oman">Tourism</a>, another source of Oman's revenue, is on the rise.<sup id="cite_ref-englishplacenames_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-englishplacenames-186">[184]</a></sup> A popular event is The Khareef Festival held in <a href="/wiki/Salalah" title="Salalah">Salalah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dhofar" class="mw-redirect" title="Dhofar">Dhofar</a>, which is 1,200&nbsp;km from the capital city of Muscat, during the monsoon season (August) and is similar to Muscat Festival. During this latter event the mountains surrounding Salalah are popular with tourists as a result of the cool weather and lush greenery, rarely found anywhere else in Oman.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[185]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Oman's <a href="/wiki/Migrant_workers_in_the_Gulf_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Migrant workers in the Gulf region">foreign workers</a> send an estimated US$10&nbsp;billion annually to their home states in Asia and Africa, more than half of them earning a monthly wage of less than US$400.<sup id="cite_ref-wsws.org_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsws.org-188">[186]</a></sup> The largest foreign community is from the Indian states of <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">Kerala</a>, Tamil Nadu, <a href="/wiki/Karnataka" title="Karnataka">Karnataka</a>, Maharashtra, <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Punjab,_India" title="Punjab, India">Punjab</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[187]</a></sup> representing more than half of entire workforce in Oman. Salaries for overseas workers are known to be less than for Omani nationals, though still from two to five times higher than for the equivalent job in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wsws.org_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsws.org-188">[186]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In terms of foreign direct investment (FDI), total investments in 2017 exceeded US$24billion. The highest share of FDI went to the oil and gas sector, which represented around US$13billion (54.2 percent), followed by <a href="/wiki/Financial_intermediary" title="Financial intermediary">financial intermediation</a>, which represented US$3.66billion (15.3 percent). FDI is dominated by the United Kingdom with an estimated value of US$11.56billion (48 percent), followed by the UAE USD 2.6billion (10.8 percent), followed by Kuwait USD 1.1billion (4.6 percent).<sup id="cite_ref-eoopaon_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eoopaon-190">[188]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px"> 
        <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black"> 
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:74.594114542418px 66.601186743425px 0 0; border-top-color:#08f"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:#08f"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:52.51746299613px 85.099448179469px 0 0; border-top-color:#008"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:#008"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:0; border-width:0 791.58150883058px 100px 0; border-right-color:silver"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;right:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 100px 0;border-color:silver"></div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption"> 
         <p>Foreign Direct Investment (FDI) in Oman by country as of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-eoopaon_190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eoopaon-190">[188]</a></sup> </p> 
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:silver; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;United Kingdom (48%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#008; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;United Arab Emirates (10.8%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#08f; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Kuwait (4.6%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:white; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Other (36.6%)
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Oman, in 2018 had a budget deficit of 32 percent of total revenue and a government debt to GDP of 47.5 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-KPMG_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KPMG-191">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OmanCEIC_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OmanCEIC-192">[190]</a></sup> Oman's military spending to GDP between 2016 and 2018 averaged 10 percent, while the world's average during the same period was 2.2 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-OMSB6a8_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OMSB6a8-193">[191]</a></sup> Oman's health spending to GDP between 2015 and 2016 averaged 4.3 percent, while the world's average during the same period was 10 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-HSIOTW_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HSIOTW-194">[192]</a></sup> Oman's research and development spending between 2016 and 2017 averaged 0.24 percent, which is significantly lower than the world's average (2.2 percent) during the same period.<sup id="cite_ref-HSRDIO_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HSRDIO-195">[193]</a></sup> Oman's government spending on education to GDP in 2016 was 6.11 percent, while the world's average was 4.8 percent (2015).<sup id="cite_ref-OMSB6a81_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OMSB6a81-196">[194]</a></sup> </p>
