      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_and_gas">Oil and gas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Oil and gas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sohar_flickr01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Sohar_flickr01.jpg/220px-Sohar_flickr01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="93" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Sohar_flickr01.jpg/330px-Sohar_flickr01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Sohar_flickr01.jpg/440px-Sohar_flickr01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3444" data-file-height="1455"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sohar_flickr01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Petrochemical tanks in <a href="/wiki/Sohar" title="Sohar">Sohar</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Oman's proved reserves of petroleum total about 5.5&nbsp;billion barrels, 25th largest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-pop_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop-141">[139]</a></sup> Oil is extracted and processed by <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_Development_Oman" title="Petroleum Development Oman">Petroleum Development Oman</a> (PDO), with proven oil reserves holding approximately steady, although oil production has been declining.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[199]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[200]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Oil_and_Gas_(Oman)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Oil and Gas (Oman)">Ministry of Oil and Gas</a> is responsible for all oil and gas infrastructure and projects in Oman.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[201]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/1970s_energy_crisis" title="1970s energy crisis">1970s energy crisis</a>, Oman doubled their oil output between 1979 and 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[202]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018, oil and gas represented 71 percent of the government's revenues.<sup id="cite_ref-KPMG_191-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KPMG-191">[189]</a></sup> In 2016, oil and gas share of the government's revenue represented 72 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-KPMG1_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KPMG1-205">[203]</a></sup> The government's reliance on oil and gas as a source of income dropped by 1 percent from 2016 to 2018. Oil and gas sector represented 30.1 percent of the nominal GDP in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-ooag_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ooag-206">[204]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Between 2000 and 2007, production fell by more than 26%, from 972,000 to 714,800 <a href="/wiki/Barrels_per_day" class="mw-redirect" title="Barrels per day">barrels per day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tnock_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tnock-207">[205]</a></sup> Production has recovered to 816,000 barrels in 2009, and 930,000 barrels per day in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-tnock_207-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tnock-207">[205]</a></sup> Oman's natural gas reserves are estimated at 849.5&nbsp;billion cubic metres, ranking 28th in the world, and production in 2008 was about 24&nbsp;billion cubic metres per year.<sup id="cite_ref-pop_141-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop-141">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In September 2019, Oman was confirmed to become the first Middle Eastern country to host the <a href="/wiki/International_Gas_Union" title="International Gas Union">International Gas Union</a> Research Conference (IGRC 2020). This 16th iteration of the event will be held between 24 and 26 February 2020, in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Oman_LNG" title="Oman LNG">Oman LNG</a>, under the auspices of the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Oil_and_Gas_(Oman)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Oil and Gas (Oman)">Ministry of Oil and Gas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[206]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Oman" title="Tourism in Oman">Tourism in Oman</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bustan-palace.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1e/Bustan-palace.jpg/220px-Bustan-palace.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1e/Bustan-palace.jpg/330px-Bustan-palace.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1e/Bustan-palace.jpg/440px-Bustan-palace.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="663"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bustan-palace.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Al-Bustan Palace Hotel
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Tourism in Oman has grown considerably recently, and it is expected to be one of the largest industries in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[207]</a></sup> The World Travel &amp; Tourism Council stated that Oman is the fastest growing tourism destination in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[208]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Tourism contributed 2.8 percent to the Omani GDP in 2016. It grew from RO 505 million (US$1.3&nbsp;billion) in 2009 to RO 719&nbsp;million (US$1.8&nbsp;billion) in 2017 (+42.3 percent growth). Citizens of the Gulf Cooperation Council (GCC), including Omanis who are residing outside of Oman, represent the highest ratio of all tourists visiting Oman, estimated to be 48 percent. The second highest number of visitors come from other Asian countries, who account for 17 percent of the total number of visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-OFIAA_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OFIAA-211">[209]</a></sup> A challenge to tourism development in Oman is the reliance on the government-owned firm, Omran, as a key actor to develop the tourism sector, which potentially creates a market <a href="/wiki/Barrier_to_entry" class="mw-redirect" title="Barrier to entry">barrier-to-entry</a> of private-sector actors and a <a href="/wiki/Crowding_out_(economics)" title="Crowding out (economics)">crowding out</a> effect. Another key issue to the tourism sector is deepening the understanding of the ecosystem and biodiversity in Oman to guarantee their protection and preservation.<sup id="cite_ref-unedp_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unedp-212">[210]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Wahiba_Sands_(33).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Wahiba_Sands_%2833%29.jpg/170px-Wahiba_Sands_%2833%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Wahiba_Sands_%2833%29.jpg/255px-Wahiba_Sands_%2833%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Wahiba_Sands_%2833%29.jpg/340px-Wahiba_Sands_%2833%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2356" data-file-height="3535"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Wahiba_Sands_(33).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Wahiba Sands
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Oman has one of the most diverse environments in the Middle East with various tourist attractions and is particularly well known for adventure and <a href="/wiki/Cultural_tourism" title="Cultural tourism">cultural tourism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-englishplacenames_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-englishplacenames-186">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[211]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Muscat" title="Muscat">Muscat</a>, the capital of Oman, was named the second best city to visit in the world in 2012 by the travel guide publisher <a href="/wiki/Lonely_Planet" title="Lonely Planet">Lonely Planet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[212]</a></sup> Muscat also was chosen as the Capital of Arab Tourism of 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[213]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In November 2019, Oman made the rule of <a href="/wiki/Travel_visa" title="Travel visa">visa</a> on arrival an exception and introduced the concept of e-visa for tourists from all nationalities. Under the new laws, visitors were required to apply for the visa in advance by visiting Oman's online government portal.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[214]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Industry.2C_innovation_and_infrastructure"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry,_innovation_and_infrastructure">Industry, innovation and infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Industry, innovation and infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In industry, innovation and infrastructure, Oman is still faced with "significant challenges", as per United Nations Sustainable Development Goals index, as of 2019. Oman has scored high on the rates of internet use, mobile broadband subscriptions, logistics performance and on the average of top 3 university rankings. Meanwhile, Oman scored low on the rate of scientific and technical publications and on research &amp; development spending.<sup id="cite_ref-UNSD3_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNSD3-125">[123]</a></sup> Oman's manufacturing value added to GDP rate in 2016 was 8.4 percent, which is lower than the average in the Arab world (9.8 percent) and world average (15.6 percent). In terms of research &amp; development expenditures to GDP, Oman's share was on average 0.20 percent between 2011 and 2015, while the world's average during the same period was 2.11 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-UNSD4_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNSD4-217">[215]</a></sup> The majority of firms in Oman operate in the oil and gas, construction and trade sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-unedp_212-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unedp-212">[210]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table class="wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Non-hydrocarbon GDP growth</th> 
         <th>2015</th> 
         <th>2016</th> 
         <th>2017</th> 
         <th>2018 </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>Value (%)<sup id="cite_ref-IMFReport_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMFReport-218">[216]</a></sup></td> 
         <td>4.8</td> 
         <td>6.2</td> 
         <td>0.5</td> 
         <td>1.5 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Oman is refurbishing and expanding the ports infrastructure in Muscat, Duqm, Sohar and Salalah to expand tourism, local production and export shares. Oman is also expanding its downstream operations by constructing a refinery and petrochemical plant in Duqm with a 230,000 barrels per day capacity projected for completion by 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-eoopaon_190-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eoopaon-190">[188]</a></sup> The majority of industrial activity in Oman takes place in 8 industrial states and 4 free-zones. The industrial activity is mainly focused on mining-and-services, petrochemicals and construction materials.<sup id="cite_ref-unedp_212-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unedp-212">[210]</a></sup> The largest employers in the private-sector are the construction, wholesale-and-retail and manufacturing sectors, respectively. Construction accounts for nearly 48 percent of the total labour force, followed by wholesale-and-retail, which accounts for around 15 percent of total employment and manufacturing, which accounts for around 12 percent of employment in the private sector. The percentage of Omanis employed in the construction and manufacturing sectors is nevertheless low, as of 2011 statistics.<sup id="cite_ref-RSIO_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RSIO-184">[182]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Oman, as per Global Innovation Index (2019) report, scores "below expectations" in innovation relative to countries classified under high income.<sup id="cite_ref-OBEII_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OBEII-219">[217]</a></sup> Oman in 2019 ranked 80 out of 129 countries in innovation index, which takes into consideration factors, such as, political environment, education, infrastructure and business sophistication.<sup id="cite_ref-romigi_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-romigi-220">[218]</a></sup> Innovation, technology-based growth and economic diversification are hindered by an economic growth that relies on infrastructure expansion, which heavily depends on a high percentage of 'low-skilled' and 'low-wage' foreign labour. Another challenge to innovation is the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_disease" title="Dutch disease">dutch disease</a> phenomenon, which creates an oil and gas investment lock-in, while relying heavily on imported products and services in other sectors. Such a locked-in system hinders local business growth and global competitiveness in other sectors, and thus impedes economic diversification.<sup id="cite_ref-unedp_212-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unedp-212">[210]</a></sup> The inefficiences and bottlenecks in business operations that are a result of heavy dependence on natural resources and 'addiction' to imports in Oman suggest a 'factor-driven economy'.<sup id="cite_ref-RSIO_184-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RSIO-184">[182]</a></sup> A third hindrance to innovation in Oman is an economic structure that is heavily dependent on few large firms, while granting few opportunities for SMEs to enter the market, which impedes healthy market-share competition between firms.<sup id="cite_ref-unedp_212-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unedp-212">[210]</a></sup> The ratio of patent applications per million people was 0.35 in 2016 and the <a href="/wiki/MENA" title="MENA">MENA</a> region average was 1.50, while the 'high-income' countries' average was approximately 48.0 during the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-WorldBankPatents_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WorldBankPatents-221">[219]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table class="wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Patent Grants</th> 
         <th>2014</th> 
         <th>2015</th> 
         <th>2016</th> 
         <th>2017 </th>
        </tr>

         <td>Total<sup id="cite_ref-PGPY_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PGPY-222">[220]</a></sup></td> 
         <td>2</td>

         <td>14 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture_and_fishing">Agriculture and fishing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Agriculture and fishing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Oman's fishing industry contributed 0.78 percent to the GDP in 2016. Fish exports between 2000 and 2016 grew from US$144&nbsp;million to US$172&nbsp;million (+19.4 percent). The main importer of Omani fish in 2016 was Vietnam, which imported almost US$80&nbsp;million (46.5 percent) in value, and the second biggest importer was the United Arab Emirates, which imported around US$26&nbsp;million (15 percent). The other main importers are Saudi Arabia, Brazil and China. Oman's consumption of fish is almost two times the world's average. The ratio of exported fish to total fish captured in tons fluctuated between 49 and 61 percent between 2006 and 2016. Omani strengths in the fishing industry comes from having a good market system, a long coastline (3,165&nbsp;km) and wide water area. Oman, on the other hand, lacks sufficient infrastructure, research and development, quality and safety monitoring, together with a limited contribution by the fishing industry to GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-OFIAA_211-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OFIAA-211">[209]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Date_(fruit)" class="mw-redirect" title="Date (fruit)">Dates</a> represent 80 percent of all fruit crop production. Further, date farms employ 50 percent of the total agricultural area in the country. Oman's estimated production of dates in 2016 is 350,000 tons, making it the 9th largest producer of dates. The vast majority of date production (75 percent) comes from only 10 cultivars. Oman's total export of dates was US$12.6&nbsp;million in 2016, almost equivalent to Oman's total imported value of dates, which was US$11.3&nbsp;million in 2016. The main importer is India (around 60 percent of all imports). Oman's date exports remained steady between 2006 and 2016. Oman is considered to have good infrastructure for date production and support provision to cultivation and marketing, but lacks innovation in farming and cultivation, industrial coordination in the supply chain and encounter high losses of unused dates.<sup id="cite_ref-OFIAA_211-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OFIAA-211">[209]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Oman" title="Demographics of Oman">Demographics of Oman</a>
      </div>
      <table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-top-width:0;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;">
       <caption style="border-top:1px #aaa solid;border-left:1px #aaa solid;border-right:1px #aaa solid;background-color:lavender;padding:0.25em;font-weight:bold">
        Historical population
       </caption>
       <tbody>
        <tr style="font-size:95%">
         <th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;width:3em">Year</th>

      <p>As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Oman's population is over 4 million, with 2.23&nbsp;million Omani nationals and 1.76&nbsp;million expatriates.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[221]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> in 2011 was estimated at 3.70.<sup id="cite_ref-mesi_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mesi-224">[222]</a></sup> Oman has a very young population, with 43 percent of its inhabitants under the age of 15. Nearly 50 percent of the population lives in <a href="/wiki/Muscat,_Oman" class="mw-redirect" title="Muscat, Oman">Muscat</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Batinah" class="mw-redirect" title="Batinah">Batinah</a> coastal plain northwest of the capital. <a href="/wiki/Omani_people" title="Omani people">Omani people</a> are predominantly of <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baloch_people" title="Baloch people">Baluchi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic groups of Africa">African</a> origins.<sup id="cite_ref-pop_141-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop-141">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Omani society is largely <a href="/wiki/Tribal" class="mw-redirect" title="Tribal">tribal</a><sup id="cite_ref-inequal_178-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inequal-178">[176]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fa_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fa-225">[223]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[224]</a></sup> and encompasses three major identities:<sup id="cite_ref-inequal_178-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inequal-178">[176]</a></sup> that of the tribe, the Ibadi faith and maritime trade.<sup id="cite_ref-inequal_178-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inequal-178">[176]</a></sup> The first two identities are closely tied to tradition and are especially prevalent in the interior of the country, owing to lengthy periods of isolation.<sup id="cite_ref-inequal_178-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inequal-178">[176]</a></sup> The third identity pertains mostly to Muscat and the coastal areas of Oman, and is reflected by business, trade,<sup id="cite_ref-inequal_178-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inequal-178">[176]</a></sup> and the diverse origins of many Omanis, who trace their roots to Baloch, <a href="/wiki/Al-Lawatia" title="Al-Lawatia">Al-Lawatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian people">Persia</a> and historical Omani <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[225]</a></sup> Consequently, the third identity is generally seen to be more open and tolerant towards others,<sup id="cite_ref-inequal_178-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inequal-178">[176]</a></sup> and is often in tension with the more traditional and insular identities of the interior.<sup id="cite_ref-inequal_178-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inequal-178">[176]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Oman" title="Islam in Oman">Islam in Oman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Oman" title="Religion in Oman">Religion in Oman</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px"> 
        <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">

         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Chartreuse"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Chartreuse"></div>

        <div class="thumbcaption"> 
         <p>Religion in Oman (2010)<sup id="cite_ref-CIATONGA_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIATONGA-228">[226]</a></sup> </p> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Green; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (85.9%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Christianity (6.5%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Orange; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> (5.5%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Chartreuse; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Others (1%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Yellow; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> (0.8%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Black; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Unaffiliated (0.2%)
