          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Blue; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Judaism (0.1%)
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Even though the Oman government does not keep statistics on religious affiliation, statistics from the US's Central Intelligence Agency state that adherents of Islam are in the majority at 85.9%, with Christians at 6.5%, Hindus at 5.5%, Buddhists at 0.8%, Jews less than 0.1%. Other religious affiliations have a proportion of 1% and the unaffiliated only 0.2%. </p>
      <p>Most Omanis are <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>, most of whom follow the <a href="/wiki/Ibadi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibadi">Ibadi</a><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[227]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Islamic_schools_and_branches" title="Islamic schools and branches">school</a> of Islam, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Twelver" title="Twelver">Twelver</a> school of <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia Islam</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Shafi%60i" class="mw-redirect" title="Shafi`i">Shafi`i</a> school of <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Islam</a>. Virtually all non-Muslims in Oman are foreign workers. Non-Muslim religious communities include various groups of <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhs</a>, Jews, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindus</a> and Christians. Christian communities are centred in the major urban areas of <a href="/wiki/Muscat,_Oman" class="mw-redirect" title="Muscat, Oman">Muscat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sohar" title="Sohar">Sohar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salalah" title="Salalah">Salalah</a>. These include <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox</a> and various <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> congregations, organising along linguistic and ethnic lines. More than 50 different Christian groups, fellowships and assemblies are active in the Muscat metropolitan area, formed by migrant workers from Southeast Asia. </p>
      <p>There are also communities of ethnic Indian <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Oman" title="Hinduism in Oman">Hindus</a> and Christians. There are also small <a href="/wiki/Sikh" class="mw-redirect" title="Sikh">Sikh</a><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[228]</a></sup> and Jewish<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[229]</a></sup> communities. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sultan_Qaboos_Highway.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Sultan_Qaboos_Highway.jpg/250px-Sultan_Qaboos_Highway.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Sultan_Qaboos_Highway.jpg/375px-Sultan_Qaboos_Highway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Sultan_Qaboos_Highway.jpg/500px-Sultan_Qaboos_Highway.jpg 2x" data-file-width="983" data-file-height="653"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sultan_Qaboos_Highway.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Arabic and English road sign in Oman
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Arabic is the official language of Oman. It belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Semitic_languages" title="Semitic languages">Semitic</a> branch of the <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">Afroasiatic</a> family.<sup id="cite_ref-molabs_181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-molabs-181">[179]</a></sup> There are several <a href="/wiki/Dialects_of_Arabic" class="mw-redirect" title="Dialects of Arabic">dialects of Arabic</a> spoken, all part of the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_Arabic" title="Peninsular Arabic">Peninsular Arabic</a> family: <a href="/wiki/Dhofari_Arabic" title="Dhofari Arabic">Dhofari Arabic</a> (also known as Dhofari, Zofari) is spoken in <a href="/wiki/Salalah" title="Salalah">Salalah</a> and the surrounding coastal regions (the <a href="/wiki/Dhofar_Governorate" title="Dhofar Governorate">Dhofar Governorate</a>);<sup id="cite_ref-e18_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-e18-232">[230]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Arabic" title="Gulf Arabic">Gulf Arabic</a> is spoken in parts bordering the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">UAE</a>; whereas <a href="/wiki/Omani_Arabic" title="Omani Arabic">Omani Arabic</a>, distinct from the Gulf Arabic of eastern Arabia and Bahrain, is spoken in Central Oman, although with recent oil wealth and mobility has spread over other parts of the Sultanate. </p>
      <p>According to the CIA, besides Arabic, English, Baluchi (Southern Baluchi), <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a> and various Indian languages are the main languages spoken in Oman.<sup id="cite_ref-pop_141-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop-141">[139]</a></sup> English is widely spoken in the business community and is taught at school from an early age. Almost all signs and writings appear in both Arabic and English at tourist sites.<sup id="cite_ref-englishplacenames_186-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-englishplacenames-186">[184]</a></sup> Baluchi is the mother tongue of the <a href="/wiki/Baloch_people" title="Baloch people">Baloch people</a> from <a href="/wiki/Balochistan" title="Balochistan">Balochistan</a> in western Pakistan, eastern <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and southern <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>. It is also used by some descendants of <a href="/wiki/Sindhi_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Sindhi people">Sindhi</a> sailors.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[231]</a></sup> A significant number of residents also speak <a href="/wiki/Urdu_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Urdu language">Urdu</a>, due to the influx of Pakistani migrants during the late 1980s and 1990s. Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a> is widely spoken in the country due to the historical relations between Oman and <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-etn.sagepub.com_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etn.sagepub.com-10">[10]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Prior to Islam, Central Oman lay outside of the core area of spoken Arabic. Possibly <a href="/wiki/Old_South_Arabian" title="Old South Arabian">Old South Arabian</a> speakers dwelled from the <a href="/wiki/Al_Batinah_Region" title="Al Batinah Region">Al Batinah Region</a> to <a href="/wiki/Zafar,_Yemen" title="Zafar, Yemen">Zafar, Yemen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[232]</a></sup> Rare <a href="/wiki/Ancient_South_Arabian_script" title="Ancient South Arabian script">Musnad</a> inscriptions have come to light in central Oman and in the Emirate of Sharjah, but the script says nothing about the language which it conveys.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[233]</a></sup> A bilingual text from the 3rd century BCE is written in Aramaic and in musnad <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hasiatic&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hasiatic (page does not exist)">Hasiatic</a>, which mentions a 'king of Oman' (mālk mn ʿmn).<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[234]</a></sup> Today the <a href="/wiki/Mehri_language" title="Mehri language">Mehri language</a> is limited in its distribution to the area around <a href="/wiki/Salalah" title="Salalah">Salalah</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Zafar,_Yemen" title="Zafar, Yemen">Zafar</a> and westward into the Yemen. But until the 18th or 19th century it was spoken further north, perhaps into Central Oman.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[235]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Baluchi_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Baluchi language">Baluchi</a> (<a href="/wiki/Southern_Baluchi_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Baluchi language">Southern Baluchi</a>) is widely spoken in Oman.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[236]</a></sup> Endangered indigenous languages in Oman include <a href="/wiki/Kumzari_language" title="Kumzari language">Kumzari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bathari_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Bathari language">Bathari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harsusi_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Harsusi language">Harsusi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hobyot_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Hobyot language">Hobyot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jibbali_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Jibbali language">Jibbali</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mehri_language" title="Mehri language">Mehri</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[237]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Omani_Sign_Language" title="Omani Sign Language">Omani Sign Language</a> is the language of the deaf community. Oman was also the first <a href="/wiki/Arab_States_of_the_Arabic_Gulf" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab States of the Arabic Gulf">Arab country in the Persian Gulf</a> to have German taught as a second language.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[238]</a></sup> The Bedouin Arabs, who reached eastern and southeastern Arabia in migrational waves—the latest in the 18th century, brought their language and rule including the ruling families of Bahrain, Qatar and the United Arab Emirates.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[239]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Oman" title="Education in Oman">Education in Oman</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="wikitable sortable floatright"> 
       <caption>
        The <a href="/wiki/Human_Capital" class="mw-redirect" title="Human Capital">Human Capital</a> Index<sup id="cite_ref-hdi_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdi-242">[240]</a></sup> 
       </caption> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Rank</th> 
         <th>Economy</th> 
         <th> score </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>56</td> 
         <td>Albania</td> 
         <td>0.62 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>55</td> 
         <td>Malaysia</td> 
         <td>0.62 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><b>54</b></td> 
         <td><b>Oman</b></td> 
         <td><b>0.62</b> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>53</td> 
         <td>Turkey</td> 
         <td>0.63 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>52</td> 
         <td>Mauritius</td> 
         <td>0.63 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Oman scored high as of 2019 on the percentage of students who complete lower secondary school and on the literacy rate between the age of 15 and 24, 99.7 percent and 98.7 percent, respectively. However, Oman's net primary school enrollment rate in 2019, which is 94.1 percent, is rated as "challenges remain" by the United Nations Sustainable Development Goals (UNSDG) standard. Oman's overall evaluation in quality of education, according to UNSDG, is 94.8 ("challenges remain") as of 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-UNSD3_125-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNSD3-125">[123]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Oman's higher education produces a surplus in humanities and liberal arts, while it produces an insufficient number in technical and scientific fields and required skill-sets to meet the market demand.<sup id="cite_ref-unedp_212-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unedp-212">[210]</a></sup> Further, sufficient human capital creates a business environment that can compete with, partner or attract foreign firms. Accreditation standards and mechanisms with a quality control that focuses on input assessments, rather than output, are areas of improvement in Oman, according to the United Nations Conference on Trade and Development 2014 report.<sup id="cite_ref-unedp_212-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unedp-212">[210]</a></sup> The transformation Index BTI 2018 report on Oman recommends that the education curriculum should focus more on the "promotion of personal initiative and critical perspective".<sup id="cite_ref-bti1_183-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bti1-183">[181]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The adult literacy rate in 2010 was 86.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-unescolit_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unescolit-243">[241]</a></sup> Before 1970, only three formal schools existed in the entire country, with fewer than 1,000 students. Since Sultan Qaboos' ascension to power in 1970, the government has given high priority to education to develop a domestic work force, which the government considers a vital factor in the country's economic and social progress. Today, there are over 1,000 state schools and about 650,000 students. </p>
      <p>Oman's first university, <a href="/wiki/Sultan_Qaboos_University" title="Sultan Qaboos University">Sultan Qaboos University</a>, opened in 1986. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Nizwa" title="University of Nizwa">University of Nizwa</a> is one of the fastest growing universities in Oman. Other post-secondary institutions in Oman include the <a href="/wiki/Higher_College_of_Technology" title="Higher College of Technology">Higher College of Technology</a> and its six branches, six colleges of applied sciences (including a teachers' training college), a college of banking and financial studies, an institute of Sharia sciences, and several nursing institutes. Some 200 scholarships are awarded each year for study abroad. </p>
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Webometrics_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Webometrics Ranking of World Universities">Webometrics Ranking of World Universities</a>, the top-ranking universities in the country are <a href="/wiki/Sultan_Qaboos_University" title="Sultan Qaboos University">Sultan Qaboos University</a> (1678th worldwide), the Dhofar University (6011th) and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Nizwa" title="University of Nizwa">University of Nizwa</a> (6093rd).<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[242]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Oman" title="Healthcare in Oman">Healthcare in Oman</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Since 2003, Oman's undernourished share of the population has dropped from 11.7 percent to 5.4 percent in 2016, but the rate remains high (double) the level of high-income economies (2.7 percent) in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-ourworld2_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ourworld2-245">[243]</a></sup> The UNSDG targets zero hunger by 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-UNSD1_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNSD1-246">[244]</a></sup> Oman's coverage of essential health services in 2015 was 77 percent, which is relatively higher than the world's average of approximately 54 percent during the same year, but lower than high-income economies' level (83 percent) in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-ourworldreport_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ourworldreport-247">[245]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since 1995, the percentage of Omani children who receive key vaccines has consistently been very high (above 99 percent). As for road incident death rates, Oman's rate has been decreasing since 1990, from 98.9 per 100,000 individuals to 47.1 per 100,000 in 2017, however, the rate remains significantly above average, which was 15.8 per 100,000 in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-UNSD2_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNSD2-248">[246]</a></sup> Oman's health spending to GDP between 2015 and 2016 averaged 4.3 percent, while the world's average during the same period averaged 10 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-HSIOTW_194-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HSIOTW-194">[192]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As for mortality due to air pollution (household and ambient air pollution), Oman's rate was 53.9 per 100,000 population as of 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-WHOREPORT_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHOREPORT-249">[247]</a></sup> In 2019, the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) ranked Oman as the least polluted country in the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a>, with a score of 37.7 in the <a href="/wiki/Air_Pollution_Index" title="Air Pollution Index">pollution index</a>. The country ranked 112th in Asia among the list of highest polluted countries.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[248]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Life expectancy at birth in Oman was estimated to be 76.1 years in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-mesi_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mesi-224">[222]</a></sup> As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were an estimated 2.1 physicians and 2.1 hospital beds per 1,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-mesi_224-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mesi-224">[222]</a></sup> In 1993, 89% of the population had access to health care services. In 2000, 99% of the population had access to health care services.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> During the last three decades, the Oman health care system has demonstrated and reported great achievements in health care services and preventive and curative medicine. Oman has been making strides in health research too recently. Comprehensive research on the prevalence of skin diseases was performed in North batinah governorate.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[249]</a></sup> In 2000, Oman's health system was ranked number 8 by the World Health Organization.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[250]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_Cities">Largest Cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Largest Cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>1) <a href="/wiki/Muscat" title="Muscat">Muscat</a> <b>(Capital City of Oman)</b>, <a href="/wiki/Muscat_Governorate" title="Muscat Governorate">Muscat Governorate</a> </p>
      <p>2) <a href="/wiki/Seeb" title="Seeb">Seeb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muscat_Governorate" title="Muscat Governorate">Muscat Governorate</a> </p>
      <p>3) <a href="/wiki/Salalah" title="Salalah">Salalah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dhofar_Governorate" title="Dhofar Governorate">Dhofar Governorate</a> </p>
      <p>4) <a href="/wiki/Bawshar" title="Bawshar">Bawshar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muscat_Governorate" title="Muscat Governorate">Muscat Governorate</a> </p>
      <p>5) <a href="/wiki/Sohar" title="Sohar">Sohar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Batinah_North_Governorate" title="Al Batinah North Governorate">Al Batinah North Governorate</a> </p>
      <p>6) As Suwayq, <a href="/wiki/Al_Batinah_North_Governorate" title="Al Batinah North Governorate">Al Batinah North Governorate</a> </p>
      <p>7) <a href="/wiki/Ibri" title="Ibri">Ibri</a>, Az Zahirah Governorate </p>
      <p>8) <a href="/wiki/Saham" title="Saham">Saham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Batinah_North_Governorate" title="Al Batinah North Governorate">Al Batinah North Governorate</a> </p>
      <p>9) <a href="/wiki/Rustaq" title="Rustaq">Rustaq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Batinah_South_Governorate" title="Al Batinah South Governorate">Al Batinah South Governorate</a> </p>
      <p>10) <a href="/wiki/Buraimi" class="mw-redirect" title="Buraimi">Buraimi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Buraimi_Governorate" title="Al Buraimi Governorate">Al Buraimi Governorate</a> </p>
      <p>11) <a href="/wiki/Nizwa" title="Nizwa">Nizwa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ad_Dakhiliyah_Governorate" title="Ad Dakhiliyah Governorate">Ad Dakhiliyah Governorate</a> </p>
      <p>12) <a href="/wiki/Sur,_Oman" title="Sur, Oman">Sur</a>, Southeastern Governorate </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Oman" title="Culture of Oman">Culture of Oman</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:DhowMuscat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/DhowMuscat.jpg/220px-DhowMuscat.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/DhowMuscat.jpg/330px-DhowMuscat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/DhowMuscat.jpg/440px-DhowMuscat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="590" data-file-height="433"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:DhowMuscat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The traditional <a href="/wiki/Dhow" title="Dhow">Dhow</a>, an enduring symbol of Oman<sup id="cite_ref-coosoo_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coosoo-253">[251]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Outwardly, Oman shares many of the cultural characteristics of its Arab neighbours, particularly those in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council" title="Gulf Cooperation Council">Gulf Cooperation Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kcom_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kcom-254">[252]</a></sup> Despite these similarities, important factors make Oman unique in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-kcom_254-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kcom-254">[252]</a></sup> These result as much from geography and history as from culture and economics.<sup id="cite_ref-kcom_254-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kcom-254">[252]</a></sup> The relatively recent and artificial nature of the <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">state</a> in Oman makes it difficult to describe a national culture;<sup id="cite_ref-kcom_254-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kcom-254">[252]</a></sup> however, sufficient cultural heterogeneity exists within its national boundaries to make Oman distinct from other Arab States of the Persian Gulf.<sup id="cite_ref-kcom_254-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kcom-254">[252]</a></sup> Oman's cultural diversity is greater than that of its Arab neighbours, given its historical expansion to the Swahili Coast and the Indian Ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-kcom_254-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kcom-254">[252]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Oman has a long tradition of shipbuilding, as maritime travel played a major role in the Omanis' ability to stay in contact with the civilisations of the ancient world. <a href="/wiki/Sur,_Oman" title="Sur, Oman">Sur</a> was one of the most famous shipbuilding cities of the Indian Ocean. The Al Ghanja ship takes one whole year to build. Other types of Omani ship include As Sunbouq and Al Badan.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[253]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In March 2016 archaeologists working off Al Hallaniyah Island identified a shipwreck believed to be that of the <i>Esmeralda</i> from <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a>'s 1502–1503 fleet. The wreck was initially discovered in 1998. Later underwater excavations took place between 2013 and 2015 through a partnership between the Oman Ministry of Heritage and Culture and <a href="/wiki/Blue_Water_Recoveries" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue Water Recoveries">Blue Water Recoveries</a> Ltd., a shipwreck recovery company. The vessel was identified through such artifacts as a "Portuguese coin minted for trade with India (one of only two coins of this type known to exist) and stone cannonballs engraved with what appear to be the initials of Vincente Sodré, da Gama's maternal uncle and the commander of the <i>Esmeralda</i>."<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[254]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dress">Dress</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Dress">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Khanjar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Khanjar.jpg/170px-Khanjar.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Khanjar.jpg/255px-Khanjar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Khanjar.jpg/340px-Khanjar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="1740"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Khanjar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Khanjar" title="Khanjar">khanjar</a>, the traditional <a href="/wiki/Dagger" title="Dagger">dagger</a> of Oman (<a href="/wiki/Circa" title="Circa">c.</a>&nbsp;1924)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The male <a href="/wiki/National_dress" class="mw-redirect" title="National dress">national dress</a> in Oman consists of the <i><a href="/wiki/Dishdasha" class="mw-redirect" title="Dishdasha">dishdasha</a></i>, a simple, ankle-length, collarless gown with long sleeves.<sup id="cite_ref-cgso_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cgso-167">[165]</a></sup> Most frequently white in colour, the dishdasha may also appear in a variety of other colours. Its main adornment, a <a href="/wiki/Tassel" title="Tassel">tassel</a> (<i>furakha</i>) sewn into the neckline, can be impregnated with perfume.<sup id="cite_ref-ossc_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ossc-257">[255]</a></sup> Underneath the dishdasha, men wear a plain, wide strip of cloth wrapped around the body from the waist down. The most noted regional differences in dishdasha designs are the style with which they are embroidered, which varies according to age group.<sup id="cite_ref-cgso_167-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cgso-167">[165]</a></sup> On formal occasions a black or beige cloak called a <a href="/wiki/Bisht_(clothing)" title="Bisht (clothing)"><i>bisht</i></a> may cover the dishdasha. The embroidery edging the cloak is often in silver or gold thread and it is intricate in detail.<sup id="cite_ref-ossc_257-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ossc-257">[255]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Omani men wear two types of headdress: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>the <i>ghutra</i>, also called "Musar" a square piece of woven wool or cotton fabric of a single colour, decorated with various embroidered patterns.</li> 
       <li>the <i>kummah</i>, a cap that is the head dress worn during leisure hours.<sup id="cite_ref-cgso_167-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cgso-167">[165]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Some men carry the <i>assa</i>, a stick, which can have practical uses or is simply used as an accessory during formal events. Omani men, on the whole, wear sandals on their feet.<sup id="cite_ref-ossc_257-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ossc-257">[255]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Khanjar" title="Khanjar">khanjar</a></i> (dagger) forms part of the national dress and men wear the khanjar on all formal public occasions and festivals.<sup id="cite_ref-cgso_167-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cgso-167">[165]</a></sup> It is traditionally worn at the waist. Sheaths may vary from simple covers to ornate silver or gold-decorated pieces.<sup id="cite_ref-ossc_257-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ossc-257">[255]</a></sup> It is a symbol of a man's origin, his manhood and courage. A depiction of a khanjar appears on the national flag.<sup id="cite_ref-cgso_167-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cgso-167">[165]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Omani women wear eye-catching national costumes, with distinctive regional variations. All costumes incorporate vivid colours and vibrant embroidery and decorations. In the past, the choice of colours reflected a tribe's tradition. The Omani women's traditional costume comprises several garments: the <i>kandoorah</i>, which is a long tunic whose sleeves or <i>radoon</i> are adorned with hand-stitched embroidery of various designs. The <i>dishdasha</i> is worn over a pair of loose fitting trousers, tight at the ankles, known as a <i><a href="/wiki/Sirwal" title="Sirwal">sirwal</a></i>. Women also wear a head shawl most commonly referred to as the <i>lihaf</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ocde_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocde-258">[256]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> women reserve wearing their traditional dress for special occasions, and instead wear a loose black cloak called an <i><a href="/wiki/Abaya" title="Abaya">abaya</a></i> over their personal choice of clothing, whilst in some regions, particularly amongst the Bedouin, the <i><a href="/wiki/Burqa" title="Burqa">burqa</a></i> is still worn.<sup id="cite_ref-ocde_258-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocde-258">[256]</a></sup> Women wear <i><a href="/wiki/Hijab" title="Hijab">hijab</a></i>, and though some women cover their faces and hands, most do not. The Sultan has forbidden the covering of faces in public office.<sup id="cite_ref-coosoo_253-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coosoo-253">[251]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_cinema">Music and cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Music and cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Music_of_Oman" title="Music of Oman">Music of Oman</a> is extremely diverse due to Oman's imperial legacy. There are over 130 different forms of traditional Omani songs and dances. The Oman Centre for Traditional Music was established in 1984 to preserve them.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[257]</a></sup> In 1985, Sultan Qaboos founded the Royal Oman Symphony Orchestra, an act attributed<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (April 2014)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> to his love for classical music. Instead of engaging foreign musicians, he decided to establish an orchestra made up of Omanis.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[258]</a></sup> On 1 July 1987 at the Al Bustan Palace Hotel's Oman Auditorium the Royal Oman Symphony Orchestra gave its inaugural concert.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[259]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sur-Cinema_(3).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Sur-Cinema_%283%29.JPG/220px-Sur-Cinema_%283%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Sur-Cinema_%283%29.JPG/330px-Sur-Cinema_%283%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Sur-Cinema_%283%29.JPG/440px-Sur-Cinema_%283%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sur-Cinema_(3).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Cinema in Sur
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Oman" title="Cinema of Oman">cinema of Oman</a> is very small, there being only one Omani film <i>Al-Boom</i> (2006) as of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. Oman Arab Cinema Company LLC is the single largest motion picture exhibitor chain in Oman. It belongs to the Jawad Sultan Group of Companies, which has a history spanning more than 40 years in the Sultanate of Oman.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[260]</a></sup> In popular music, a seven-minute music video about Oman went viral, achieving 500,000 views on YouTube within 10 days of being released on YouTube in November 2015. The a cappella production features three of the region's most popular talents: Kahliji musician Al Wasmi, Omani poet Mazin Al-Haddabi and actress Buthaina Al Raisi.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[261]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The government has continuously held a monopoly on television in Oman. <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Oman_Television" title="Sultanate of Oman Television">Oman TV</a> is the only state-owned national television channel broadcaster in Oman. It began broadcasting for the first time from Muscat on 17 November 1974 and separately from <a href="/wiki/Salalah" title="Salalah">Salalah</a> on 25 November 1975. On 1 June 1979, the two stations at Muscat and Salalah linked by satellite to form a unified broadcasting service. Oman TV broadcasts four HD channels, including Oman TV General, Oman TV Sport, Oman TV Live and Oman TV Cultural.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[262]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although private ownership of radio and television stations is permitted, Oman has only one privately owned television channel.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-265">[263]</a></sup> Majan TV is the first private TV channel in Oman. It began broadcasting in January 2009. However, Majan TV's official channel website was last updated in early 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[264]</a></sup> Moreover, the public has access to foreign broadcasts since the use of satellite receivers is allowed.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_265-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-265">[263]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[265]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Oman Radio is the first and only state-owned radio channel.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_265-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-265">[263]</a></sup> It began broadcasting on the 30th, July 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[266]</a></sup> It operates both Arabic and English networks. Other private channels include Hala FM, Hi FM, Al-Wisal, Virgin Radio Oman FM and Merge. In early 2018, Muscat Media Group (MMG), trend-setting media group founded by late Essa bin Mohammed Al Zedjali, launched a new private radio stations in hopes of catering educative and entertaining programmes to the youth of the Sultanate.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[267]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[268]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[269]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Oman has nine main newspapers, five in Arabic and four in English.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[270]</a></sup> Instead of relying on sales or state subsidies, private newspapers depend on advertising revenues to sustain themselves.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-273">[271]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The media landscape in Oman has been continuously described as restrictive, censored, and subdued.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[272]</a></sup> The Ministry of Information censors politically, culturally, or sexually offensive material in domestic or foreign media. The press freedom group <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a> ranked the country 127th out of 180 countries on its 2018 World Press Freedom Index. In 2016, the government drew international criticism for suspending the newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Azamn" title="Azamn">Azamn</a></i> and arresting three journalists after a report on corruption in the country's judiciary. <a href="/wiki/Azamn" title="Azamn">Azamn</a> was not allowed to reopen in 2017 although an appeal court ruled in late 2016 that the paper can resume operating.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_273-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-273">[271]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Traditional art in Oman stems from its long heritage of material culture. Art movements in the 20th century reveal that the art scene in Oman began with early practices that included a range of tribal handicrafts and self-portraiture in painting since the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[273]</a></sup> However, since the inclusion of several Omani artists in international collections, art exhibitions, and events, such Alia Al Farsi, the first Omani artist to show at the last <a href="/wiki/Venice_Biennale" title="Venice Biennale">Venice Biennale</a> and Radhika Khimji, the first Omani artist to exhibit at both the <a href="/wiki/Arts_in_Marrakech_(AiM)_International_Biennale" title="Arts in Marrakech (AiM) International Biennale">Marrakesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ghetto_Biennale" title="Ghetto Biennale">Haiti Ghetto biennale</a>, Oman's position as a newcomer to the contemporary art scene in recent years has been more important for Oman's international exposure.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-276">[274]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:324px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Aflaj_Gallery_in_The_National_Museum_Oman,.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Aflaj_Gallery_in_The_National_Museum_Oman%2C.jpg/322px-Aflaj_Gallery_in_The_National_Museum_Oman%2C.jpg" decoding="async" width="322" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Aflaj_Gallery_in_The_National_Museum_Oman%2C.jpg/483px-Aflaj_Gallery_in_The_National_Museum_Oman%2C.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Aflaj_Gallery_in_The_National_Museum_Oman%2C.jpg/644px-Aflaj_Gallery_in_The_National_Museum_Oman%2C.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3942" data-file-height="1697"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Aflaj_Gallery_in_The_National_Museum_Oman,.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ancient irrigation system and water channels.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[275]</a></sup> Aflaj Gallery, The National Museum of Oman.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bait Muzna Gallery is the first art gallery in Oman. Established in 2000 by Sayyida Susan Al Said, Bait Muzna has served as a platform for emerging Omani artists to showcase their talent and place themselves on the wider art scene. In 2016, Bait Muzna opened a second space in <a href="/wiki/Salalah" title="Salalah">Salalah</a> to branch out and support <a href="/wiki/Art_film" title="Art film">art film</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Digital_art" title="Digital art">digital art</a> scene. The gallery has been primarily active as an art consultancy.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_276-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-276">[274]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[276]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Sultanate's flagship cultural institution, the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_(Oman)" title="National Museum (Oman)">National Museum of Oman</a>, opened on 30 July 2016 with 14 permanent galleries. It showcases national heritage from the earliest human settlement in Oman two million years ago through to the present day. The museum takes a further step by presenting information on the material in <a href="/wiki/Arabic_Braille" title="Arabic Braille">Arabic Braille</a> script for the visually impaired, the first museum to do this in the Gulf region.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_276-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-276">[274]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Omani Society for Fine Arts, established in 1993, offers educational programmes, workshops and artist grants for practitioners across varied disciplines. In 2016, the organisation opened its first exhibition on graphic design. It also hosted the "Paint for Peace" competition with 46 artists in honour of the country's 46th <a href="/wiki/National_Day_of_Oman" title="National Day of Oman">National Day</a>, where Mazin al-Mamari won the top prize. The organisation has additional branches in <a href="/wiki/Sohar" title="Sohar">Sohar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Buraimi_Governorate" title="Al Buraimi Governorate">Buraimi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salalah" title="Salalah">Salalah</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_276-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-276">[274]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Bait_Al_Zubair" title="Bait Al Zubair">Bait Al- Zubair Museum</a> is a private, family-funded museum that opened its doors to the public in 1998. In 1999, the museum received <a href="/wiki/Qaboos_bin_Said_al_Said" class="mw-redirect" title="Qaboos bin Said al Said">Sultan Qaboos</a>’ Award for Architectural Excellence. Bait Al Zubair displays the family's collection of Omani artifacts that spans a number of centuries and reflect inherited skills that define Oman's society in the past and present. Located within Bait Al-Zubair, Gallery Sarah, which opened in October 2013, offers an array of paintings and photographs by established local and international artists. The gallery also occasionally holds lectures and workshops.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[277]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Food">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Omani_cuisine" title="Omani cuisine">Omani cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Traditional_Omani_Food.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Traditional_Omani_Food.jpg/220px-Traditional_Omani_Food.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Traditional_Omani_Food.jpg/330px-Traditional_Omani_Food.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Traditional_Omani_Food.jpg/440px-Traditional_Omani_Food.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3216" data-file-height="2136"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Traditional_Omani_Food.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Traditional Omani food
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Omani cuisine is diverse and has been influenced by many cultures. Omanis usually eat their main daily meal at midday, while the evening meal is lighter. During <a href="/wiki/Ramadan" title="Ramadan">Ramadan</a>, dinner is served after the <a href="/wiki/Taraweeh" class="mw-redirect" title="Taraweeh">Taraweeh</a> prayers, sometimes as late as 11&nbsp;pm. However, these dinner timings differ according to each family; for instance, some families would choose to eat right after <a href="/wiki/Maghrib" class="mw-redirect" title="Maghrib">maghrib</a> prayers and have dessert after taraweeh. </p>
      <p>Arsia, a festival meal served during celebrations, consists of mashed rice and meat (sometimes chicken). Another popular festival meal, shuwa, consists of meat cooked very slowly (sometimes for up to 2 days) in an underground clay oven. The meat becomes extremely tender and it is infused with spices and herbs before cooking to give it a very distinct taste. Fish is often used in main dishes too, and the <a href="/wiki/Giant_trevally" title="Giant trevally">kingfish</a> is a popular ingredient. Mashuai is a meal consisting of a whole spit-roasted kingfish served with lemon rice. </p>
      <p>Rukhal bread is a thin, round bread originally baked over a fire made from palm leaves. It is eaten at any meal, typically served with Omani honey for breakfast or crumbled over curry for dinner. Chicken, fish, and lamb or mutton are regularly used in dishes. The Omani <a href="/wiki/Halva" title="Halva">halwa</a> is a very popular sweet, basically consisting of cooked raw sugar with nuts. There are many different flavors, the most popular ones being black halwa (original) and saffron halwa. Halwa is considered as a symbol of Omani hospitality, and is traditionally served with coffee. As is the case with most <a href="/wiki/Arab_states_of_the_Persian_Gulf" title="Arab states of the Persian Gulf">Arab states of the Persian Gulf</a>, alcohol is only available over-the-counter to non-Muslims. Muslims can still purchase alcoholic drinks. Alcohol is served in many hotels and a few restaurants. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Oman" class="mw-redirect" title="Sport in Oman">Sport in Oman</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MuscatGulfCup2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/MuscatGulfCup2.jpg/220px-MuscatGulfCup2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/MuscatGulfCup2.jpg/330px-MuscatGulfCup2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/MuscatGulfCup2.jpg/440px-MuscatGulfCup2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="819" data-file-height="614"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MuscatGulfCup2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Oman hosted and won the <a href="/wiki/19th_Arabian_Gulf_Cup" title="19th Arabian Gulf Cup">19th Arabian Gulf Cup</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In October 2004, the Omani government set up a <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ministry_of_Sports_Affairs&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ministry of Sports Affairs (page does not exist)">Ministry of Sports Affairs</a> to replace the General Organisation for Youth, Sports and Cultural Affairs. The <a href="/wiki/19th_Arabian_Gulf_Cup" title="19th Arabian Gulf Cup">19th Arabian Gulf Cup</a> took place in <a href="/wiki/Muscat,_Oman" class="mw-redirect" title="Muscat, Oman">Muscat</a>, from 4 to 17 January 2009 and was won by the <a href="/wiki/Oman_national_football_team" title="Oman national football team">Omani national football team</a>. The <a href="/wiki/23rd_Arabian_Gulf_Cup" title="23rd Arabian Gulf Cup">23rd Arabian Gulf Cup</a> that took place in <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, from 22 December 2017 until 5 January 2018 with <a href="/wiki/Oman_national_football_team" title="Oman national football team">Oman</a> winning their second title, defeating the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_national_football_team" title="United Arab Emirates national football team">United Arab Emirates</a> in the final on penalties following a goalless draw. </p>
      <p>The first "<a href="/wiki/El_Cl%C3%A1sico" title="El Clásico">El Clasico</a>" to be played outside of Spain, was played on March 14, 2014 at the <a href="/wiki/Sultan_Qaboos_Sports_Complex" title="Sultan Qaboos Sports Complex">Sultan Qaboos Sports Complex</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[278]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF" title="Real Madrid CF">Real Madrid F.C.</a> starting eleven consisted of: Contreras, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%ADchel_Salgado" title="Míchel Salgado">Míchel Salgado</a>, Pavón, Belenguer, Fernando Sanz, Velasco, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Hierro" title="Fernando Hierro">Fernando Hierro</a>, De la Red, Amavisca, Sabido and Alfonso. Emilio Álvarez, García Cortés, Torres Mestre, Morán, Álex Pérez, and Iván Pérez also played. <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a> played with: Felip, Coco, Roberto, Nadal, Goicochea, Milla, <a href="/wiki/V%C3%ADctor_Mu%C3%B1oz" title="Víctor Muñoz">Víctor Muñoz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gaizka_Mendieta" title="Gaizka Mendieta">Gaizka Mendieta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludovic_Giuly" title="Ludovic Giuly">Giuly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Ezquerro" title="Santiago Ezquerro">Ezquerro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luis_Garc%C3%ADa_(footballer,_born_1978)" title="Luis García (footballer, born 1978)">Luis García</a>. Moner, Ramos, Albert Tomás, Mulero, Arpón, Lozano and Christiansen also played. The match ended with a score of 2 to 1 in favor of FC Barcelona. </p>
      <p>Oman's traditional sports are <a href="/wiki/Dhow" title="Dhow">dhow</a> racing, <a href="/wiki/Horse_racing" title="Horse racing">horse racing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Camel_racing" title="Camel racing">camel racing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bull_fighting" class="mw-redirect" title="Bull fighting">bull fighting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Falconry" title="Falconry">falconry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Your_Middle_East_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Your_Middle_East-281">[279]</a></sup> Association football, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waterskiing" class="mw-redirect" title="Waterskiing">waterskiing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sandboarding" title="Sandboarding">sandboarding</a> are among the sports that have emerged quickly and gained popularity among the younger generation.<sup id="cite_ref-Your_Middle_East_281-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Your_Middle_East-281">[279]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Ali_Al-Habsi" title="Ali Al-Habsi">Ali Al-Habsi</a> is an Omani professional association football player. As of 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, he plays in the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Championship">Football League Championship</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Goalkeeper_(football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Goalkeeper (football)">goalkeeper</a> for <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Brom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[280]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> awarded<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (April 2014)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> the former GOYSCA its prestigious prize for Sporting excellence in recognition of its contributions to youth and sports and its efforts to promote the Olympic spirit and goals. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_tpower1978_-_World_Cup_Qualifiers_(7).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Flickr_-_tpower1978_-_World_Cup_Qualifiers_%287%29.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_tpower1978_-_World_Cup_Qualifiers_%287%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Flickr_-_tpower1978_-_World_Cup_Qualifiers_%287%29.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_tpower1978_-_World_Cup_Qualifiers_%287%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Flickr_-_tpower1978_-_World_Cup_Qualifiers_%287%29.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_tpower1978_-_World_Cup_Qualifiers_%287%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_tpower1978_-_World_Cup_Qualifiers_(7).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>2010 FIFA World Cup Qualifiers Round 3 match between <a href="/wiki/Oman_national_football_team" title="Oman national football team">Oman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japan_national_football_team" title="Japan national football team">Japan</a> at the Royal Oman Police Stadium on 7 June 2008 in Muscat, Oman
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Oman_Olympic_Committee" title="Oman Olympic Committee">Oman Olympic Committee</a> played a major part in organising the highly successful 2003 Olympic Days, which were of great benefit to the sports associations, clubs, and young participants. The <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> association took part, along with the <a href="/wiki/Handball" title="Handball">handball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sport_of_athletics" title="Sport of athletics">athletics</a>, swimming and <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> associations. In 2010 Muscat hosted the <a href="/wiki/2010_Asian_Beach_Games" title="2010 Asian Beach Games">2010 Asian Beach Games</a>. </p>
      <p>Oman also hosts tennis tournaments in different age divisions each year. The <a href="/wiki/Sultan_Qaboos_Sports_Complex" title="Sultan Qaboos Sports Complex">Sultan Qaboos Sports Complex</a> stadium contains a 50-meter swimming pool which is used for international tournaments from different schools in different countries. The Tour of Oman, a professional cycling 6-day stage race, takes place in February. Oman hosted the Asian <a href="/wiki/2011_FIFA_Beach_Soccer_World_Cup_qualification_(AFC)" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 FIFA Beach Soccer World Cup qualification (AFC)">2011 FIFA Beach Soccer World Cup qualifiers</a>, where 11 teams competed for three spots at the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Beach_Soccer_World_Cup" title="FIFA Beach Soccer World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a>. Oman hosted the Men's and Women's <a href="/wiki/2012_Beach_Handball_World_Championships" title="2012 Beach Handball World Championships">2012 Beach Handball World Championships</a> at the Millennium Resort in Mussanah, from 8 to 13 July.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[281]</a></sup> Oman has competed repeatedly for a position in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a>, but have yet qualified to compete in the tournament. </p>
      <p>Oman, along with <a href="/wiki/Fujairah" title="Fujairah">Fujairah</a> in the <a href="/wiki/UAE" class="mw-redirect" title="UAE">UAE</a>, are the only regions in the Middle East that have a variant of <a href="/wiki/Bullfighting" title="Bullfighting">bullfighting</a>, known as 'bull-butting', organised within their territories.<sup id="cite_ref-rg_bull_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rg_bull-284">[282]</a></sup> Al-Batena area in Oman is specifically prominent for such events. It involves two bulls of the <a href="/wiki/Brahman_(cattle)" class="mw-redirect" title="Brahman (cattle)">Brahman</a> breed pitted against one another and as the name implies, they engage in a forceful barrage of headbutts. The first one to collapse or concede its ground is declared the loser. Most bull-butting matches are short affairs and last for less than 5 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-rg_bull_284-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rg_bull-284">[282]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[283]</a></sup> The origins of bull-butting in Oman remain unknown, but many locals believe it was brought to Oman by the Moors of Spanish origin. Yet others say it has a direct connection with <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, which colonised the Omani coastline for nearly two centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">[284]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a>, Oman qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2016_ICC_World_Twenty20" title="2016 ICC World Twenty20">2016 ICC World Twenty20</a> by securing sixth place in <a href="/wiki/2015_ICC_World_Twenty20_Qualifier" title="2015 ICC World Twenty20 Qualifier">2015 ICC World Twenty20 Qualifier</a>. They have also been granted T20I status as they were among the top six teams in the qualifiers. On 30 October 2019, they qualified for 2020 T20 Cricket World Cup which will be hosted by Australia. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa 1px;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style>
      <div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright"> 
       <ul> 
        <li><span><img alt="flag" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Oman.svg/32px-Flag_of_Oman.svg.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="16" class="noviewer thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Oman.svg/48px-Flag_of_Oman.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Oman.svg/64px-Flag_of_Oman.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600"></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Oman" title="Portal:Oman">Oman portal</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div>

       <li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_Oman" title="Outline of Oman">Outline of Oman</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Index_of_Oman-related_articles" title="Index of Oman-related articles">Index of Oman-related articles</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style>
      <div class="reflist"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-66"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-66">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1783, when Seyyid Said succeeded to the "masnad" of Muscat and Oman (an independent state founded in 1749), he fell out with his brother Imam Sultan, who fled to safety in Makran and entered into communication with Nasir Khan of Kalat. Said was granted the Kalat share of the revenues of Gwadar and lived there until 1797 when he came to rule over Muscat and Oman.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-91"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-91">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Gwadar remained an Omani possession as part of the Sultanate until September 1958</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>
